  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fbd9aaa2-be34-4509-ba2a-a4e053fa60ae'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9626533543737880643"><b>Millions of readers have discovered the magic of David Eddings' <i>New</i> <i>York Times</i> bestselling series <i>The Belgariad</i>. Now the first three books in this monumental epic appear in a single volume. Here, long-time fans can rediscover the wonder--and the uninitiated can embark upon a thrilling new journey of fantasy and adventure. </b><br/><br/>It all begins with the theft of the Orb that for so</span>
  <span id="freeText9626533543737880643" style="display:none"><b>Millions of readers have discovered the magic of David Eddings' <i>New</i> <i>York Times</i> bestselling series <i>The Belgariad</i>. Now the first three books in this monumental epic appear in a single volume. Here, long-time fans can rediscover the wonder--and the uninitiated can embark upon a thrilling new journey of fantasy and adventure. </b><br /><br />It all begins with the theft of the Orb that for so long protected the West from an evil god. As long as the Orb was at Riva, the prophecy went, its people would be safe from this corrupting power. Garion, a simple farm boy, is familiar with the legend of the Orb, but skeptical in matters of magic. Until, through a twist of fate, he learns not only that the story of the Orb is true, but that he must set out on a quest of unparalleled magic and danger to help recover it. For Garion is a child of destiny, and fate itself is leading him far from his home, sweeping him irrevocably toward a distant tower--and a cataclysmic confrontation with a master of the darkest magic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9626533543737880643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1167164876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1167164876" />
    <a title="Christopher Paolini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33610695-christopher-paolini"><img alt="Christopher Paolini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591638018p2/33610695.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1167164876?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christopher Paolini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christopher Paolini" href="/user/show/33610695-christopher-paolini">Christopher Paolini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33610695-christopher-paolini?shelf=stories-that-inspired-my-books">stories-that-inspired-my-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33610695-christopher-paolini?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1167164876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11321329306479540389">My grandfather on my father’s side bought me <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/291354.The_Ruby_Knight__The_Elenium___2_' title='The Ruby Knight (The Elenium, #2) by David Eddings' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Ruby Knight</a>
</i>—the second book in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68806.The_Elenium_The_Diamond_Throne___The_Ruby_Knight___The_Sapphire_Rose__The_Elenium___1_3_' title='The Elenium The Diamond Throne / The Ruby Knight / The Sapphire Rose (The Elenium, #1-3) by David Eddings' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Elenium trilogy</a>, by David Eddings—when I was nine or ten. It was the first modern fantasy I had ever read, and I remember being utterly captivated by Mr. Eddings’ story of knights and magic and monsters, and thinking, “I <i>like</i> this!”<br/><br/>I liked it so much, in fact, that I raced to our local library and, over the course of several months, devoured every novel Mr. Eddings had published. I even went so far as to purc</span>
  <span id="freeText11321329306479540389" style="display:none">My grandfather on my father’s side bought me <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/291354.The_Ruby_Knight__The_Elenium___2_" title="The Ruby Knight (The Elenium, #2) by David Eddings" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ruby Knight</a>
</i>—the second book in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68806.The_Elenium_The_Diamond_Throne___The_Ruby_Knight___The_Sapphire_Rose__The_Elenium___1_3_" title="The Elenium The Diamond Throne / The Ruby Knight / The Sapphire Rose (The Elenium, #1-3) by David Eddings" rel="nofollow noopener">The Elenium trilogy</a>, by David Eddings—when I was nine or ten. It was the first modern fantasy I had ever read, and I remember being utterly captivated by Mr. Eddings’ story of knights and magic and monsters, and thinking, “I <i>like</i> this!”<br /><br />I liked it so much, in fact, that I raced to our local library and, over the course of several months, devoured every novel Mr. Eddings had published. I even went so far as to purchase all five books of the series.<br /><br />Mr. Eddings’ The Belgariad series (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18878.The_Belgariad__Vol__1_Pawn_of_Prophecy___Queen_of_Sorcery___Magician_s_Gambit__The_Belgariad___1_3_" title="The Belgariad, Vol. 1 Pawn of Prophecy / Queen of Sorcery / Magician's Gambit (The Belgariad, #1-3) by David Eddings" rel="nofollow noopener">Volume One</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18879.The_Belgariad__Vol__Two_Castle_of_Wizardry___Enchanters__End_Game__The_Belgariad___4_5_" title="The Belgariad, Vol. Two Castle of Wizardry / Enchanters' End Game (The Belgariad, #4-5) by David Eddings" rel="nofollow noopener">Volume Two</a>) is a wonderful introduction to fantasy. A classic coming-of-age epic, it features a young farm boy with a mysterious past; a mad, twisted god for a villain; true love; thrilling duels and battles; a unique land; and some of the most interesting characters in the genre. Mr. Eddings influenced how I approach fantasy, both as a reader and as an author. The Belgariad will always have a place of honor on my bookshelves.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11321329306479540389" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_68678182" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68678182" />
    <a title="Lorena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/251417-lorena"><img alt="Lorena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489184320p2/251417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68678182?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lorena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lorena" href="/user/show/251417-lorena">Lorena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251417-lorena?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68678182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11179704841168790787">Maybe more like a 2.75 on the ratings scale. Competent but predictable fantasy. The author created the world before he created the story, and it shows. The setting is very thoroughly imagined and meticulously crafted; the story, less so. The characters are all familiar fantasy archetypes, though not bad examples of those archetypes, for the most part. The pacing is exceedingly slow, and the action depends a great deal on the people in the story not telling each other basic, necessary information</span>
  <span id="freeText11179704841168790787" style="display:none">Maybe more like a 2.75 on the ratings scale. Competent but predictable fantasy. The author created the world before he created the story, and it shows. The setting is very thoroughly imagined and meticulously crafted; the story, less so. The characters are all familiar fantasy archetypes, though not bad examples of those archetypes, for the most part. The pacing is exceedingly slow, and the action depends a great deal on the people in the story not telling each other basic, necessary information about what they are doing or why, which gets tiresome. You would think that, by the forty-eleventh time the Prophesied Savior Of The Whole Universe is nearly killed because his "wise" mentors gave him a necklace and said, "Here, put this on, it's a family tradition to wear one" instead of "You must wear this magical medallion at all times and never ever take it off even to bathe or else the forces of evil will CONTROL YOUR MIND," it might clue them in that perhaps a more thorough explanation of what is going on might be in order. But no. Apparently not. <br /><br />There are two more books in the series, contained in the next omnibus, which I do plan on reading. If only to see if it is ever explained why our hero, who is destined to do battle with the Ultimate Evil, and whose upbringing was strictly under the control of his "wise mentors," was never taught seemingly basic stuff like...how to read. And how to fight with a sword. Or any other weapon, really. Perhaps the next volumes will explain why our hero was raised in such a way as to make him seemingly incompetent to walk to the next village and buy a spool of thread on his own, much less fight an ultimate battle for the fate of the world. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11179704841168790787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11994214778673747043" style="display:none">Queen of Sorcery is definitely still my favorite. There's so much humor in this series. <div id="review_1288664215" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1288664215" />
    <a title="Maddy Lanslots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42625743-maddy-lanslots"><img alt="Maddy Lanslots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430330265p2/42625743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1288664215?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddy Lanslots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddy Lanslots" href="/user/show/42625743-maddy-lanslots">Maddy Lanslots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42625743-maddy-lanslots?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42625743-maddy-lanslots?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288664215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10210711637944742545">This is the fourth time I'm reading the Belgariad series by Eddings and I will never stop loving it. The worst thing that could be said about these books is that they are a tad predictable, the characters somewhat stereotypical, and that it is rather "light" for a fantasy series; but I think that is why I enjoy it so much. It makes these books suitable for a wide range of ages. I first read it when I was in my early/middle teens and I noticed that I read it differently each time, noticing differ</span>
  <span id="freeText10210711637944742545" style="display:none">This is the fourth time I'm reading the Belgariad series by Eddings and I will never stop loving it. The worst thing that could be said about these books is that they are a tad predictable, the characters somewhat stereotypical, and that it is rather "light" for a fantasy series; but I think that is why I enjoy it so much. It makes these books suitable for a wide range of ages. I first read it when I was in my early/middle teens and I noticed that I read it differently each time, noticing different and new things.<br /><br />The story is your typical quest: Garion, a young farm boy, is basically dragged out of his safe and familiar environment one night by his Aunt Pol and an old storyteller, Mr Wolf, for - to him - unknown purposes. As their journey progresses and more companions join their small group, Garion slowly starts to learn more about the reason for their quest and eventually finds out that he has a part to play in it, too.<br /><br />The books are written in a third-person narrative, but they are almost completely told from Garion's point of view; what Garion does not know, the reader also does not know (with the exception of the respective prologues of each separate book in this series, which serve to give the reader background information about the world and the history thereof). The world-building is amazing, in my opinion - very detailed, making it easy for the reader to imagine the world in his head, but it is not described so extensively that it becomes tiresome.<br /><br />The characters are, despite sometimes following certain stereotypes (both with regard to races, such as "all Arends are stupid" and "all Tolnedrans are obsessed with money", and in the sense of familiar-seeming character types being included, such as the characters of the strong knight, the spoilt princess, the wise sorcerer, etc.), well-developed and generally likable. Some parts are very funny - I laughed out loud more than once whilst reading this book, even for the fourth time - whilst others keep you on the edge of your seat or even manage to evoke some emotional response.<br /><br />All in all, I think these books are amazing and I would recommend them to every fan of fantasy and/or adventure stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10210711637944742545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11738575939767990719">Get ready for the overuse of the word "sardonic" and characters who absolutely have to have the last word ("oh, really?" "yes, indeed!" "I thought you might feel that way." "I was born feeling this way.") I have to be loyal to a fellow Reedie, but Eddings takes the easy way out too often, merely stating situations when he could take more pains to show them ("The young boy took her hand with a mournful look in his eyes showing profound love, tinged with hope and fear and a midafternoon's hunger f</span>
  <span id="freeText11738575939767990719" style="display:none">Get ready for the overuse of the word "sardonic" and characters who absolutely have to have the last word ("oh, really?" "yes, indeed!" "I thought you might feel that way." "I was born feeling this way.") I have to be loyal to a fellow Reedie, but Eddings takes the easy way out too often, merely stating situations when he could take more pains to show them ("The young boy took her hand with a mournful look in his eyes showing profound love, tinged with hope and fear and a midafternoon's hunger for a good meat pie.") I want to make it clear that I enjoyed the Belgariad and the Mallorean. I just don't really know if I would recommend them to anyone I know right now.     </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154394049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11468342522786318311">This is my review for both David Eddings series Belgariad and The Malloreon I know it is a little long but bear with me please. As a warning there will be spoilers.<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>The Belgariad and The Malloreon series has truly struck a cord whith me in a way that no series has been able to do since The Sword of Truth series and before that The Harry Potter series. Both of the authors of those series had a special power to take what they had written and bring it alive withing the pages. This is what David Eddi</span>
  <span id="freeText11468342522786318311" style="display:none">This is my review for both David Eddings series Belgariad and The Malloreon I know it is a little long but bear with me please. As a warning there will be spoilers.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />The Belgariad and The Malloreon series has truly struck a cord whith me in a way that no series has been able to do since The Sword of Truth series and before that The Harry Potter series. Both of the authors of those series had a special power to take what they had written and bring it alive withing the pages. This is what David Eddings has done for me in his books. I know that early in my reading of this series I compared it to The Lord of the Rings series but after finishing it I have come to a new conculusion while some of it is in fact similer and I am sure that David Eddings like all other authors was influenced slightly by Tolkien's work but Eddings is vastly difforent where Tolkien spent most of his time developing his world Eddings dedicated his stories to developing his characters and he sure did. The characters in his novels are much more human much more relatable than some of Tolkein's seemingly invulnerable characters they have truly human flaws weaknesses and fears the characters in LOTR tend to not have much in the way of thoes normal realatable human characteristics. This is one of the main things that drew me to his story. David Eddings also manages to have many very strong very prominent female characters throughout his series this was one of the things that LOTR lacked more than any other it simply has almost no female characters and while this may work for some types of fiction it doesn't for fantasy. For what is fantasy with out some romance and love? Just a silly children's fairy tale. ( I must make it perfectly clear that I am not calling LOTR one such story the work that Tolkien put into is simply astonishing but it is lacking in some major areas. But it's okay because it worked for him and I did enjoy the books. ) I found I liked David Eddings work more than Tolkien's also because its just a fantastic story in and of itself while some parts may drag a bit and some werent givin as much time a we thought they deserved but this is true of all works of righting the author does there best to satasfy all of their readers and David Eddings lives up to that satisfaction. I will not be stoping after these two series I fully intend to read every book that David Eddings and his wife have written and I am sure that I will be much happier for it. I strongly recomend David Eddings work to all lovers of fantasy this series of his was able to keep me going for almost two weeks and I am sure that you all will be able to get at least some enjoyment out of them as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11468342522786318311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText2435956081194698462" style="display:none">This Fantasy series is entertaining. Some of the dialogue is witty and sharp. Clearly there's ideas lifted from Tolkein - it's hard to find fantasy that can't be traced back to Tolkein. However, there's more character driven plots than JRR which makes for a fun read.<br />With some tweaking this could actually be adapted to film. Sometimes the characters bleed into one another.   <span id="freeText6419276951467771569" style="display:none">This series has been recommended to me more times than I can count. I finally got around to reading it and I gotta say... not sure what all the fuss is about. I mean, it was good, but it wasn't any better in my opinion than any of those other series out there that tell the same tale- good vs. evil, magic vs. non-magic, follow the prophecy road... you get the idea. This book fits the formula to a T. I could tell you everything that was going to happen in this series by the second chapter. What I couldn't tell you were the characters' reactions. What made this book a four star one was (as with most books of this formula) the supporting cast. I just loved the characters who surround our hero, though I'm fairly lukewarm on the hero himself.</span>

  <span id="freeText10498244331472978915" style="display:none">Either I'm getting old or I've read this series too many times, but the first half at least didn't give me the comforting warm and fuzzies I was expecting from this re-read.<br /><br />I mean, they were still there: the characters and passages I remember cherishing as a kid. They seemed changed somehow, though, emptier than before. I found myself bored in the interim.<br /><br />The women, of course, get little to do in these first three books. Belgarath disparages Garion for not listening to Polgara after showing example of never listening to her himself.<br /><br />What I will grant is that Eddings does make his world come to life, simplistic though it might be. <div id="review_66750802" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66750802" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1229405-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1248560462p2/1229405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66750802?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/1229405-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1229405-jennifer?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1229405-jennifer?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66750802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16095139890178272214">The flippant dialogue is at first charming, then predictable, and ultimately mind-numbing and/or entirely inappropriate given the situation. The plot is an interminable travelogue of new places and characters, only briefly developed, in service to Eddings' fleshing out the maps he drew before writing this series (see Eddings' Preface in this volume). Worse, the plot is furthered in no small way simply by characters not telling each other what is obviously important information (not just to the r</span>
  <span id="freeText16095139890178272214" style="display:none">The flippant dialogue is at first charming, then predictable, and ultimately mind-numbing and/or entirely inappropriate given the situation. The plot is an interminable travelogue of new places and characters, only briefly developed, in service to Eddings' fleshing out the maps he drew before writing this series (see Eddings' Preface in this volume). Worse, the plot is furthered in no small way simply by characters not telling each other what is obviously important information (not just to the reader, but also to them as characters within their more limited perceptions)--a cheap and easy device not worthy of Eddings' talents in other respects, even though he does a better job of grounding it rationally than most who take this "easy out."<br /><br />Still, I wasn't ready to throw this compendium down until I was three-quarters done (2 and 1/3 books, roughly), so I finished it. Eddings has a strong eye for interesting detail and much of these novels is well written, despite their overall insufficiencies. Too, the interplay between mythology and real-time is intriguing.<br /><br />Bottom line, they are financially motivated, hack-work at its best--which is higher praise than it sounds like. If you are new to fantasy or need a diverting beach read, by all means check it out of the library. Don't buy it though--you won't ever reread it like you might Hobbs or Martin for their characters or Bishop or Zelazny for their unique worlds.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16095139890178272214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4702091746742937688" style="display:none">This first volume of the Belgariad is a decently engaging story, but not one I would recommend to others. Under different circumstances, we might even have been friends." There's also some fairly distasteful racist undercurrents. In the end, there is the obligatory fleeing from the villain's lair which collapses into ruin as soon as he is defeated for completely arbitrary reasons. Still, I can think of worse ways to waste a few hours.</span>

<div id="review_141550067" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/141550067" />
    <a title="Evan Wondrasek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4826452-evan-wondrasek"><img alt="Evan Wondrasek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516141789p2/4826452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/141550067?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evan Wondrasek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evan Wondrasek" href="/user/show/4826452-evan-wondrasek">Evan Wondrasek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4826452-evan-wondrasek?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4826452-evan-wondrasek?shelf=would-read-again">would-read-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141550067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13681485734956365208">This was really exciting to re-read, because this is the first series of novels I remember reading independently as a kid. I don't remember all of the details anymore, but when I was pretty young, my mom picked up the first book in this series (Pawn of Prophecy), and I read it cover-to-cover and loved it. Mom kept going to the book store and picking up the next book in the series until I had read all of The Belgariad, then all of The Mallorean, and then all of the standalone books like the ones </span>
  <span id="freeText13681485734956365208" style="display:none">This was really exciting to re-read, because this is the first series of novels I remember reading independently as a kid. I don't remember all of the details anymore, but when I was pretty young, my mom picked up the first book in this series (Pawn of Prophecy), and I read it cover-to-cover and loved it. Mom kept going to the book store and picking up the next book in the series until I had read all of The Belgariad, then all of The Mallorean, and then all of the standalone books like the ones about Belgarath and Polgara, and the Rivan Codex. And then all of a sudden, I was out of books, so Mom dutifully went back to the book store and asked for help, and what did they introduce us to? The Lord of the Rings. Yeah, life got real good around this time.<br /><br />Anyway, I really haven't read much fantasy in my life, aside from David Eddings and JRR Tolkien. But for years, I've always daydreamed about going back and re-reading The Belgariad series, part out of nostalgia, and part out of curiosity about what it would be like to re-read these books as an adult -- would they hold up? Would they be too childish?<br /><br />I started re-reading the first book in the series, Pawn of Prophecy, on my old, yellowed trade paperback version that I had as a kid. Unfortunately, I wasn't able to find the other 4 books in The Belgariad from my original collection, so I went out and picked up this new omnibus volume which they call The Belgariad, Vol. 1, which contains the first 3 books from the series, and Vol. 2 contains the last two books in the series. It was nice reading in a larger format than the trade paperback (and nice having those clean white pages), but one downside was that the hand-drawn maps were poorly scanned from the originals and were quite blurry. (Also, very minor, this omnibus collection features "a new foreword from the author", which was 1 light page of someone essentially saying "oh hey glad this was popular, haroomph").<br /><br />So, my conclusions after finishing Vol. 1: It was super enjoyable re-reading these as an adult. The weren't childish at all -- I'm guessing I didn't fully understand everything as a kid, but it goes to show that kids and adults can read the same books and still get something good from them. I remembered several things quite vividly, but overall, I had forgotten most of the details of the story, so it was fun going on the journey again with a fresh mind. I can't objectively rate this book from a story and quality of writing perspective, because there's too much nostalgic noise in the way, but I enjoyed reading it and I'm going to start Vol 2. very soon. And realistically, I'll probably keep reading all of the follow-up books as well.<br /><br />And then maybe I'll finally get around to re-reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110692.The_Redemption_of_Althalus?from_search=true&amp;qid=VNc33y9wrN&amp;rank=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Redemption of Althalus</a>, which was my so-called favorite book as a kid...</span>
  <a data-text-id="13681485734956365208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2320515735" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2320515735" />
    <a title="Ian Hardee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65784316-ian-hardee"><img alt="Ian Hardee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489093967p2/65784316.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320515735?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian Hardee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian Hardee" href="/user/show/65784316-ian-hardee">Ian Hardee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65784316-ian-hardee?shelf=read-fantasy">read-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320515735" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18245603263809832507">*there are some extremely minor spoilers as to when certain things are revealed to the main character in the books in this review, these things are, however, are revealed in the prologue, so EXTREMELY minor*<br/><br/>I'm enjoying this book immensely. I'm not even done with it, and yet I'm here to let you know that. I've just finished book two, and I felt the need to come and write this. <br/><br/>I was conflicted on starting this because the reviews are so disparate. So I wanted to write a review to sort some thing</span>
  <span id="freeText18245603263809832507" style="display:none">*there are some extremely minor spoilers as to when certain things are revealed to the main character in the books in this review, these things are, however, are revealed in the prologue, so EXTREMELY minor*<br /><br />I'm enjoying this book immensely. I'm not even done with it, and yet I'm here to let you know that. I've just finished book two, and I felt the need to come and write this. <br /><br />I was conflicted on starting this because the reviews are so disparate. So I wanted to write a review to sort some things out. <br /><br />I have loved this book. It has some flaws, some of them very painful, but if you have the fortitude and the understanding, I think you'll like this. <br /><br />So first, the bad. There are a certain caste of books I refer to as the "second &amp; third generation" fantasy books. Those writing just after Tolkien and Lewis. Second and Third Generation fantasy writers tend to introduce their concepts much slower. To us this is an issue, but I always keep in mind that, at the time, their audience was not as fluent in magic systems and fantasy races, etc, etc, and that these concepts were more unique and new. So I take that slowness with a grain of salt. Eddings has this understanding going for him, and yet it STILL bothers me. Why? Because Eddings takes TWO BOOKS. ALMOST TWO ENTIRE BOOKS to get to Garion's powers AT ALL. That's too much guys. Even considering the time period he was writing it. And he's late third generation. And whats worse, he told you exactly who Garion was IN THE PROLOGUE OF THE FIRST BOOK. There were two solutions to this. Either don't tell us, thus removing the sense of tension we get waiting on what we already know to be revealed to Garion, or reveal his powers to him before the end of the first book. But Eddings waited until the end of the second book to show him anything, and here the reader is waiting for soooo long that the excitement has spoiled. It just becomes annoying. You don't cheer when Garion uses his power for the first time, you say "Finally. Goodness gracious". <br /><br />So why, then, I hear you ask, have you given this book a five star rating? Because this book is like a stone that I've kept in my pocket for many years. When I picked it up it was because I was sick of many of the modern grimdark fantasy books I had tried of late and just wanted something that was completely, honestly just the hero story I longed for. And that is where Eddings excels. If you are looking for something off the wall and new, don't buy this book. But if you're looking for a sturdy fantasy that can take the weight of needing to be everything you want in a fantasy book, BUY IT. There's magic, eternal sorcerers, gods, rogues, barbarians, swamps and snake people, heck, there's in entire country that's just full of Arthurian stereotypes. Like that stone, this story is by no means new. All the edges have been worn off by the love people have shown to it through imitation over the years but that gives it this magical smooth feeling that just makes me happy when I read it. <br /><br />So, in conclusion here some reasons you SHOULDN'T buy this book.<br /><br />1. If you are looking for something that is going to blow your mind with new ideas and concepts.<br /><br />2. If you want the characters to struggle REALLY hard. <br /><br />3. If you can't survive two books without a full explanation of the magic system. <br /><br />4. If you want something that is the slightest bit gritty.<br /><br />Here are some reasons you SHOULD buy this book.<br /><br />1. If you are looking for a true blue fantasy. <br /><br />2. If you are looking for fun characters and fun settings and plots. <br /><br />3. If you want an interesting take on sorcerers and the exact opposite of every "wise wizard" in your general fantasy literature. Belgarath CAN be an idiot, and I kind of dig it. <br /><br />4. If you're sick and tired of looking for a good fantasy, and just want something you can rely on to be a ton of fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18245603263809832507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1063507961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1063507961" />
    <a title="Morgan Beldyk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10998330-morgan-beldyk"><img alt="Morgan Beldyk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475686771p2/10998330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1063507961?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan Beldyk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan Beldyk" href="/user/show/10998330-morgan-beldyk">Morgan Beldyk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1063507961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10911053440760452311">I really want to like this book. It was very pleasant to read. The author is good at description without getting bogged down in it, and the plot moves quickly without being confusing. The book, however, is extremely flawed and highly unoriginal. If you're looking for a unique take on the "Ordinary Farm Boy is the Chosen One to Save the World" story, you'll have to look elsewhere, because this follows the template completely unironically.<br/><br/>The characters were likable, but somewhat flat. Everyone ha</span>
  <span id="freeText10911053440760452311" style="display:none">I really want to like this book. It was very pleasant to read. The author is good at description without getting bogged down in it, and the plot moves quickly without being confusing. The book, however, is extremely flawed and highly unoriginal. If you're looking for a unique take on the "Ordinary Farm Boy is the Chosen One to Save the World" story, you'll have to look elsewhere, because this follows the template completely unironically.<br /><br />The characters were likable, but somewhat flat. Everyone has only one or two personality characteristics that drive everything they do. Worse, every race in the world is driven by one or two characteristics, and the characters we meet are just cardboard cutouts of their race's templates. It was very dull and borderline offensive to continually read about how "This race is stupid," and "This race is evil." Also the good guys -- the *good guys* -- were openly advocating genocide of the "evil" race, and one character gleefully tries to kill every one he meets. They don't even attempt to justify the violence and stereotyping by saying "These are dwarves" and "These are orcs;" no, these are all races of humans. <br /><br />Perhaps even more frustrating is the world. Two of the characters are revealed to be five thousand years old. In those five thousand years, magic has waxed and waned, cities have risen and fallen, but the overall technological level of the world has remained the same. For reference, in five thousand years humans on Earth went from the ancient Babylonian civilization to present day. Are we really expected to believe that the humans on this world maintained a Generic Medieval European setting for this amount of time? </span>
  <a data-text-id="10911053440760452311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1463919437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1463919437" />
    <a title="Berry Muhl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20111112-berry-muhl"><img alt="Berry Muhl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367890559p2/20111112.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1463919437?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Berry Muhl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Berry Muhl" href="/user/show/20111112-berry-muhl">Berry Muhl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1463919437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10212065068002386382">I'll offer the same review for both volumes of this book. I didn't read the individual novels as they were published; my first encounter with Eddings took place via the collected series.<br/><br/>Short version: a funny, scary, adventurous, deep story, told well.<br/><br/>Long version: if you've only read a few fantasy series, as I have, it's hard to pigeonhole this. It's not as horrific as Terry Goodkind's novels, but still much more graphic than Tolkien's. I find myself comparing it to the LOTR trilogy, and coming</span>
  <span id="freeText10212065068002386382" style="display:none">I'll offer the same review for both volumes of this book. I didn't read the individual novels as they were published; my first encounter with Eddings took place via the collected series.<br /><br />Short version: a funny, scary, adventurous, deep story, told well.<br /><br />Long version: if you've only read a few fantasy series, as I have, it's hard to pigeonhole this. It's not as horrific as Terry Goodkind's novels, but still much more graphic than Tolkien's. I find myself comparing it to the LOTR trilogy, and coming up with this.<br /><br />It's built on the same reluctant-hero-on-a-quest-to-save-the-world-from-unimaginable-evil-via-ancient-artifact blueprint. There's the same kind of merging of myth and history, unified in heroic legends, although it's not nearly as deep or detailed as Tolkien (and that's probably a good thing for the casual reader). This is an altogether lighter read than any of the LOTR books, and it doesn't build to the same kind of dread. But it is perhaps more personal, with the relationships and personality quirks front and center at all times. The characters are lively, and their banter revealing.<br /><br />I consider this a good starter series for the fantasy novice. For five books you get about as much reading as Tolkien's three. There's about the same amount of exposition before things truly get underway; right about the time you start to wonder when something is going to happen, something happens, and keeps on happening.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10212065068002386382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_6919984" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6919984" />
    <a title="Johnny Feng" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/418366-johnny-feng"><img alt="Johnny Feng" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

        rated it

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/418366-johnny-feng?shelf=advisorybooks">advisorybooks</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6919984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8966591045571526071">David Eddings begins each book with a piece of history pretaining to the land. We focus on the journey of a young boy by the name of Garion as he is forced to flee his home along with his aunt Pol and travel on a long journey to retrieve a stolen object of great importance. As they journey across multiple countries in pursuit of the object, we see Garion develop his latent powers and we end the third book with the return to where everything began. </span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150016018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1617692896568519667">This is a high-brow fantasy novel. Eddings has created a new world with its own complex history. I am not a fan of such fantasy because I often find trying to remember the history of a made up world to be really tedious. Trying to keep three thousand years of kings and drama straight was more than I wanted. I didn't even finish this novel. It cam highly recommended by one of my friends, but I couldn't get interested in any of the characters or the plot.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6508311?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Solitairerose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Solitairerose" href="/user/show/332346-solitairerose">Solitairerose</a>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer18197806902073483359">Average fantasy with a few flourishes. Reading it now, it reads almost like an adaptation of a Japanese Fantasy RPG where the minute you see a map, you know the characters will have to go to every named point on it, and once they have, the series is over. It's pleasantly written, and the writing style moves pretty briskly. Fun fantasy fluff that goes on a bit too long.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1040421033" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1040421033" />
    <a title="Gabriel Vidrine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3277503-gabriel-vidrine"><img alt="Gabriel Vidrine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460500793p2/3277503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1040421033?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabriel Vidrine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabriel Vidrine" href="/user/show/3277503-gabriel-vidrine">Gabriel Vidrine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3277503-gabriel-vidrine?shelf=too-awful-to-finish">too-awful-to-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1040421033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9696124885658862220">This is another book I really wanted to like. I enjoy high fantasy, even cliched high fantasy. But there was little to recommend in this one. Other authors and other series do everything in this one better. Maybe I would have liked this one had I read it before all the other fantasy I've read. I made a valiant attempt at finishing it, even going well beyond my normal 100 page limit (if it sucks after 100 pages, I don't waste any more time on it) in hopes that it would get better. But I just coul</span>
  <span id="freeText9696124885658862220" style="display:none">This is another book I really wanted to like. I enjoy high fantasy, even cliched high fantasy. But there was little to recommend in this one. Other authors and other series do everything in this one better. Maybe I would have liked this one had I read it before all the other fantasy I've read. I made a valiant attempt at finishing it, even going well beyond my normal 100 page limit (if it sucks after 100 pages, I don't waste any more time on it) in hopes that it would get better. But I just couldn't do it.<br /><br />If you want the politics, go for Game of Thrones or Feist.<br />If you want interesting characters and adventure, go for Dragonlance or Tolkien.<br />If you want the Magical Thingy that Everyone Is Looking For, go for Tolkien or Brooks.<br />If you want war, go for Feist.<br />If you want undeveloped and uninteresting women and White Men Who Solve Everything, go for Feist.<br /><br />Eddings seems to have taken the worst of cliched fantasy and put it in this series. There is little plot, little character development (when it does happen you are beaten over the head with it), and an overabundance of names of places, things, and history. All the names are similar enough that it's hard to differentiate them (Grolims are bad guys, but Gorims are apparently friends of Belgarath, though it's not explained who they are). The history dump at the beginning of each novel is difficult to follow because of the massive number of people, races, and places that are mentioned but never explained or developed (how can we care about or remember who the Asturians are if they aren't on the map and we don't even know who they are or what they stand for?)<br /><br />Let's tackle the plot first, then move on to other problems with the series. Where is the plot? At first, the three major characters seem to be running around the countryside trying to keep Garion away from someone, which makes some amount of sense. But nope, they're actually <br />chasing something...and they bring along a useless fourteen year old boy along with them (yeah, yeah, who is "secretly" the King in waiting...yet everyone knows it but him...not much of a secret). And that's about it. They're chasing a thief and have a King in waiting. A scavenger hunt combined with a game of keep away is not my idea of an engaging plot.<br /><br />On to the rest of the problems.<br /><br />Let's not even get into the racism inherent in the entire series. Or wait, let's. There's nothing wrong with putting racism in a book - it's a real thing that all people struggle with and it's naive to think it has no place in fantasy. But at least make it a character flaw or something to struggle against in the plot, especially if it's in all the main characters. Racism is bad, y'all, so let's not glorify/normalize it by not pointing it out as a flaw if all your characters have it. But all the characters are blatantly, unrepentantly racist (ALL of them), tossing out sentences like, "Oh, <br />he's a so-and-so race, they don't think very fast so don't bother explaining things to him." Wow. Later, there is even internalized racism. One character basically admits he's an idiot just because of his race. Double wow.<br /><br />Let's move on to the characters.<br /><br />Garion should have been named Right Place, Right Time, because he manages to hear every single conversation that is supposed to be private and finds all of the sneaking bad guys. If he goes off alone, you can bet your life savings that he's about to overhear something <br />important. He also manages to say just the right, wise things to the right people to move the story forward, though he's a fourteen year old farmer boy, and has skills in hunting and fighting that he shouldn't have (some mysterious force overtakes him and suddenly he's a warrior). It's either that, or his companions (and all the bad guys) are incompetent, always holding private conversations next to crumbling walls or without checking for listeners first. Either way, lazy writing.<br /><br />I don't necessarily mind fantasy that has few women in it, nor do I demand strong women in every novel I read. But if you're going to bother putting a "strong" woman into the story, at least make her actually strong. We are beaten over the head, constantly, over how strong and regal Polgara is supposed to be, but what does she do all the time? She sews, cooks, nags (and overprotects) Garion, and defers to her father. Strong? No, I don't think so. If the author wanted a camp follower for the characters, go ahead and do that, but at least do us women a favor and don't keep telling us she's such a strong, regal woman. It's not the fact that Polgara fulfills the camp follower role that's bothersome, but that the author makes such a point that Pol is strong, and regal, and not a servant to anyone - there are even conversations about that very thing in the novel. And yet she is either a demure mother figure that overprotects and holds back Garion and does all the camp chores with no help at all or a vindictive harpy who holds grudges for centuries (and attacks a blind woman for telling the truth). So the usual Whore/Madonna role for women has been replaced by a Wholesome Mother/Bitch Queen duality. Not much of an upgrade. And yes, Pol really does all the cooking with no help. It's even pointed out in one chapter where everyone else is literally standing around watching her cook. Come on, guys...strong women are more than that. A strong woman can cook and sew...but she can also <br />do other things, too. And get the men off their lazy butts to help a lady out.<br /><br />There is too much telling, not enough showing, throughout the entire novel. In only two pages, Garion meets a new character, Lelldorin, and becomes instant best friends with him because he is so trustworthy, open, and interesting (and how does Garion know this? Apparently, the author told him). The author even tells us (again, doesn't show us) that Garion has known Lelldorin long enough to know lots of things about him, yet, according to the story, they've only known each other overnight, a matter of hours! That's only one example of this grievous problem. It's everywhere in the book, and it gets worse as it goes along. <br /><br />And finally...sourly. Please, Mr. Eddings, find another adverb.<br /><br />In all, a weak, predictable story filled with racism, sexism, and boring, weak, Mary Sue characters. Nice maps, though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9696124885658862220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer5596100119467807445">DNF. This was given to me as a Christmas present a few years ago and I only just got around to picking it up. I tried to slough through it for something like two months and got halfway through before I gave up. This is a mediocre remix of the successful elements of epic fantasies like LOTR, told in a sloppy and unoriginal manner. The characters travel from place to place to place and encounter the exact same hardships in each one. Plus Garion is exceptionally unintelligent. Except when he's not.</span>
  <span id="freeText5596100119467807445" style="display:none">DNF. This was given to me as a Christmas present a few years ago and I only just got around to picking it up. I tried to slough through it for something like two months and got halfway through before I gave up. This is a mediocre remix of the successful elements of epic fantasies like LOTR, told in a sloppy and unoriginal manner. The characters travel from place to place to place and encounter the exact same hardships in each one. Plus Garion is exceptionally unintelligent. Except when he's not. Because he has a magic voice in his head that tells him deeply profound things, which he trots out at exactly the right time to make everyone around him marvel at how extraordinary he is. Lastly, don't even get me started on the sexism. Overall, a dull, uninspired story whose best elements even leave something to be desired.<br /><br />I can usually get through a horrible or dull book if I at least have a character who holds my fascination and I want to see what becomes of them. Silk almost was that character for me, if only he had been more than a cardboard cutout of a rogue archetype, and if the plot wasn't so predictable that I could guess from page 2 where it was going.</span>

<div id="review_2420771108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2420771108" />
    <a title="Shelly L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38761322-shelly-l"><img alt="Shelly L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551570094p2/38761322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2420771108?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly L" href="/user/show/38761322-shelly-l">Shelly L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38761322-shelly-l?shelf=100_npr_top_sci-fy">100_npr_top_sci-fy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2420771108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4511160798694573673">It is known that a young hero-to-be must first live to see puberty. Training he must have, at the right times and with the right techniques. And grow he must, healthy of body and mind, without taint of knowing his potential for absolute power that corrupts so absolutely. And thus, oh motherless child of destiny, you shall be granted an auntie. Counterintuitive as may be, it is always of help to the omnipotent forces that wind the web of the universe to put an Aunt Pol on the case. A worthy aunti</span>
  <span id="freeText4511160798694573673" style="display:none">It is known that a young hero-to-be must first live to see puberty. Training he must have, at the right times and with the right techniques. And grow he must, healthy of body and mind, without taint of knowing his potential for absolute power that corrupts so absolutely. And thus, oh motherless child of destiny, you shall be granted an auntie. Counterintuitive as may be, it is always of help to the omnipotent forces that wind the web of the universe to put an Aunt Pol on the case. A worthy auntie, charged to make your protection her sacred duty. A wise woman who shall suffer no fools, your Aunt Pol. Lo, as you will eventually be shook to learn, your Aunt Pol has awesome powers beyond your imagining. Powers that enable her to cure the blind at a word, or take the form of an owl at her will. But, never you worry. As good women will, she shall hide her (magic) light beneath a bushel basket (of potatoes), all to protect you, golden boy. Rather than statecraft or leadership roles, your auntie will deploy her considerable might in delicious cooking and devoted childcare. Do not think for a moment, oh male child, that mischief-making gambits will defeat your auntie's watchful eye. No matter how many pots she has on the boil, Aunt Pol will prevail, as prevail she must for the fate of our very existence. Aunt Pol will forgo lofty station, her very sleep or comfort, and of course, any thought of romantic companionship. Yea shall she serve as single mother unto you, and you alone. Her satisfactions shall be simple: keeping you safe, teaching you humility, and never faltering in her dedication to the cause. This renowned beauty will rebuff all suitors, just as she has done for more than three hundred years, awaiting your very birth. Though it will be (annoyingly) notable how much she enjoys bathing, dressing up, and being complimented on her beauty by really any man at all. But tut, tut, no matter and no more. You must know NOTHING 'til your adventure begins. And once it (eventually) begins, never fear. Aunt Pol, though revealed as the legendary Sorceress Polgara, will STILL ensure that you, and everyone in your traveling party, get fed. And I do mean every single day, in all weathers, over various campfires or what-have-you. She will STILL tend to any and all aches or pains or sword cuts or boo boos you may bring her, as the lot of you traipse all over the map for (inscrutable) reasons that shall remain (frustratingly) unclear. Yes, she may begin bathing a bunch and wearing more finery, and will sometimes turn into an owl in the night. Yes, she will be forever backtalking her dad — yes, yes, I shouldn't be telling you this, but he's your sorcerer (great, great, etc.) grandpa — per his centuries of boozing and womanizing and ridiculously flawed, plot-gear-grinding plans. But whatever else happens, have no fear, my boy. She'll still be your good old, protective-to-over-controlling, steely-eyed yet stereotypically feminine, probably (secretly) quite horny, gender-rolled and easy to take for granted, Aunt Pol.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4511160798694573673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_201329426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201329426" />
    <a title="Paul Lunger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5859124-paul-lunger"><img alt="Paul Lunger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353803965p2/5859124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201329426?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Lunger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Lunger" href="/user/show/5859124-paul-lunger">Paul Lunger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201329426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9865692272463823670">The first book in "The Belgariad" series begins the tale of Garion a boy raised in the kingdom of Saldaria by his Aunt Pol who is protecting him from a past he may not want to know of. Eddings spins a tale across both this kingdom & Cherek as we learn piece-by-piece the details of our characters lives as he introduces us to a world of magic & mystery. Throughout it as characters are slowly introduced the story keeps moving at a pace that is easy enough for the reader to enjoy & also to follow wi</span>
  <span id="freeText9865692272463823670" style="display:none">The first book in "The Belgariad" series begins the tale of Garion a boy raised in the kingdom of Saldaria by his Aunt Pol who is protecting him from a past he may not want to know of. Eddings spins a tale across both this kingdom &amp; Cherek as we learn piece-by-piece the details of our characters lives as he introduces us to a world of magic &amp; mystery. Throughout it as characters are slowly introduced the story keeps moving at a pace that is easy enough for the reader to enjoy &amp; also to follow without getting bogged down in details. It also helps that in the places where the plot needs to advance Eddings does so in a way that keeps the reader involved. The first half of the book sets the majority of the background work for the moving of the story the Cherek where the second half of the story picks up. It's there that we learn more or less the details of essentially who our cast of characters are &amp; also more about the forces of evil at work in this kingdom. For a first book in a fantasy series this is one of the easier ones I've read in a while &amp; hopefully the trend will continue throughout.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9865692272463823670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_342536843" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/342536843" />
    <a title="Matthew Cirilli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9758625-matthew-cirilli"><img alt="Matthew Cirilli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403300286p2/9758625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/342536843?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Cirilli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Cirilli" href="/user/show/9758625-matthew-cirilli">Matthew Cirilli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer342536843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12045913108772792338">This seems like the beginning of a truly epic fantasy series. I'm tempted to give it 5 stars, but I think that I might need to keep reading the series to see if it really ends up deserving that. The book is a classic fantasy story with a LOT borrowed from Tolkien. I guess that isn't really a bad thing since most fantasy is rooted in him, but some of it is a bit too obvious. <br/><br/>Regardless, Eddings does an awesome job with character development and world building. He gives a very straightforward myth</span>
  <span id="freeText12045913108772792338" style="display:none">This seems like the beginning of a truly epic fantasy series. I'm tempted to give it 5 stars, but I think that I might need to keep reading the series to see if it really ends up deserving that. The book is a classic fantasy story with a LOT borrowed from Tolkien. I guess that isn't really a bad thing since most fantasy is rooted in him, but some of it is a bit too obvious. <br /><br />Regardless, Eddings does an awesome job with character development and world building. He gives a very straightforward mythology to start with and also includes plenty of maps. It's clear that a lot of thought went into the world creation and it shows. The story is maybe a bit slow to start and it focuses on Garion (the main character) at a young age a first. Once he starts to grow up the second part of the book really steps up the action.<br /><br />It's also nice to have a fantasy story that isn't 900 so pages long. This first book was only 262 pages, which makes for a nice little read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12045913108772792338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_997642122" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/997642122" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5532305-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517174155p2/5532305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/997642122?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/5532305-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer997642122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4813616415428697871">I read the first three books in succession. All I can say is, what a refreshing story. Eddings does an excellent job of carrying the story. Every time I put the book down I couldn't wait until the next time I picked it up. The story involves the typical fantasy characters such as sorcerers, elves, dwarves and the like, but it also includes some rare ones that I've not seen in any stories I've read. Many involve names of made up creatures I cannot remember, but Dryads are one set of creatures tha</span>
  <span id="freeText4813616415428697871" style="display:none">I read the first three books in succession. All I can say is, what a refreshing story. Eddings does an excellent job of carrying the story. Every time I put the book down I couldn't wait until the next time I picked it up. The story involves the typical fantasy characters such as sorcerers, elves, dwarves and the like, but it also includes some rare ones that I've not seen in any stories I've read. Many involve names of made up creatures I cannot remember, but Dryads are one set of creatures that I do recall. I thought this was going to be a Lord of the Rings clone but surprisingly, Eddings has created a tale that is very much unlike LOTR, which is great. I cannot wait to read the last two books in the installment, and from there I will see what else Eddings has in store for me to read.<br /></span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0w5ECov/Vs+OX/FUF4qoDVJyxB30OijTeAtUlfDN+Snf5gZadeB1Lk/yDB++L6YZgWwwAc2RoYScz9Qr5vuaIA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dZ9AT2GPIBOA4tUKmRP9FudOsSTgO6NK6p3MHMX7dF95dwIfn5AD8kFPKEEwtvMCNFBFONmQKh0OWUyi080XVg==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8732.David_Eddings">About David Eddings</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8732.David_Eddings"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1223870462p3/8732.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8732.David_Eddings">David Eddings
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,767
followers

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10242273800375441672">David Eddings was an American author who wrote several best-selling series of epic fantasy novels. David Eddings' wife, <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8732.Leigh_Eddings' title='Leigh Eddings' rel='nofollow noopener'>Leigh Eddings</a>
</b>, was an uncredited co-author on many of his early books, but he had later acknowledged that she contributed to them all.<br/><br/>David Eddings' first books (which were general fiction) sold moderately well. He later switched to writing epic fantasy, a field in which he a</span>
  <span id="freeText10242273800375441672" style="display:none">David Eddings was an American author who wrote several best-selling series of epic fantasy novels. David Eddings' wife, <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8732.Leigh_Eddings" title="Leigh Eddings" rel="nofollow noopener">Leigh Eddings</a>
</b>, was an uncredited co-author on many of his early books, but he had later acknowledged that she contributed to them all.<br /><br />David Eddings' first books (which were general fiction) sold moderately well. He later switched to writing epic fantasy, a field in which he achieved great success. In a recent interview with sffworld.com, he said: "I don't take orders from readers."<br /><br />On January 26, 2007 it was reported that Eddings accidentally burned about a quarter of his office, next door to his house, along with his Excalibur sports car, and the original manuscripts for most of his novels. He was flushing the fuel tank of the car with water when he lit a piece of paper and threw into the puddle to test if it was still flammable.<br /><br />On February 28, 2007, David Eddings' wife, Leigh Eddings (born Judith Leigh Schall), died following a series of strokes. She was 69.<br /><br />David Eddings died on June 2, 2009 at the age of 77.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10242273800375441672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
